- task_completion: Task was completed only in a capability-limited contracted form. - task_understanding: Collect low-cost, macro-level structural evidence from the provided (prepared) molecular structure relevant to the TICT hypothesis versus ICT: specifically (a) whether the scaffold shows clear donor–acceptor (charge-transfer) partitioning potential for S1 and (b) whether there are plausible aryl/heteroaryl torsional “gates” whose twisting could strongly modulate conjugation and thus S1 energy/brightness. Stay within deterministic topology/geometry-proxy analysis using shared_structure_context; no excited-state calculations or aggregate modeling.

- reasoning_summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a very large, mostly polyaryl/olefinic conjugated system (101 atoms; 10 aromatic rings; 10 rotatable bonds) containing a single small heteroaromatic unit with 3 hetero atoms (nsnc fused-like motif in the canonical SMILES). Topologically, this provides (i) an extended conjugated pathway with many phenyl substituents (consistent with ICT-capable delocalization) and (ii) multiple rotatable aryl–aryl/aryl–vinyl junctions that can decouple subunits upon twisting (a prerequisite for TICT-like conformational control). However, the available proxies indicate high overall planarity (planarity_proxy ~0.97) for the selected conformer, suggesting the chosen geometry is largely conjugation-preserving rather than strongly twisted; this weakens direct structural support for a strongly twisted emissive S1 at that geometry, though it does not rule out TICT if alternate conformers access larger torsions (rotatable_bond_count=10; conformer_count=10; conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0 indicates conformational variability exists but is not quantified here). Donor/acceptor partition proxy is moderate (~0.5) and hetero atom count is low (3 total), implying only a modest built-in electronic asymmetry: CT may be present but not strongly enforced by classic strong donor/acceptor substituents. Net macro-evidence: the scaffold has several torsional degrees of freedom near aryl junctions and around the heteroaromatic attachment that could enable TICT-like modulation, but the current low-cost indicators (high planarity; modest DA proxy; low hetero count) are at least equally consistent with an ICT-like, broadly delocalized excited state unless specific key torsions are shown to be large in relevant conformers.
Capability limit note: This macro pass can only use the provided structure context (counts and geometry proxies) and SMILES-level topology to flag whether TICT is structurally plausible (rotatable junctions + donor/acceptor segmentation cues). It cannot compute excited-state CT metrics, oscillator strengths, or torsion-dependent spectra; it also cannot perform new conformer/torsion searches beyond the provided summary.

- execution_plan: Use deterministic_macro_structure_scan to execute the bounded macro workflow with focus areas: Topology: count/placement of rotatable bonds and aryl junctions; presence and position of heteroaromatic unit, DA partition cues: hetero atom count and localization; donor/acceptor partition proxy; overall symmetry vs asymmetry from SMILES connectivity, Geometry proxies: planarity_proxy, compactness_proxy, principal_span_proxy, conformer_count/dispersion as a proxy for accessible torsional diversity. Planned local steps: [shared_context_load] Load the shared prepared structure context and reuse its descriptors. [focus_selection] Select the macro structural focus areas requested by the Planner instruction. [topology_analysis] Summarize rotor topology, ring systems, conjugation, and donor-acceptor layout. [geometry_proxy_analysis] Summarize planarity, torsion, compactness, and conformer-dispersion proxies.

Reasoning summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a very large, mostly polyaryl/olefinic conjugated system (101 atoms; 10 aromatic rings; 10 rotatable bonds) containing a single small heteroaromatic unit with 3 hetero atoms (nsnc fused-like motif in the canonical SMILES). Topologically, this provides (i) an extended conjugated pathway with many phenyl substituents (consistent with ICT-capable delocalization) and (ii) multiple rotatable aryl–aryl/aryl–vinyl junctions that can decouple subunits upon twisting (a prerequisite for TICT-like conformational control). However, the available proxies indicate high overall planarity (planarity_proxy ~0.97) for the selected conformer, suggesting the chosen geometry is largely conjugation-preserving rather than strongly twisted; this weakens direct structural support for a strongly twisted emissive S1 at that geometry, though it does not rule out TICT if alternate conformers access larger torsions (rotatable_bond_count=10; conformer_count=10; conformer_dispersion_proxy=1.0 indicates conformational variability exists but is not quantified here). Donor/acceptor partition proxy is moderate (~0.5) and hetero atom count is low (3 total), implying only a modest built-in electronic asymmetry: CT may be present but not strongly enforced by classic strong donor/acceptor substituents. Net macro-evidence: the scaffold has several torsional degrees of freedom near aryl junctions and around the heteroaromatic attachment that could enable TICT-like modulation, but the current low-cost indicators (high planarity; modest DA proxy; low hetero count) are at least equally consistent with an ICT-like, broadly delocalized excited state unless specific key torsions are shown to be large in relevant conformers.

### Round 3 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=ICT (0.45) vs top2=TICT (0.29). Latest evidence does not add new mechanistic discrimination because the intended microscopic torsion-snapshot screen failed again at contract parsing (bond-type literal mismatch), so ICT is not newly strengthened by fresh data; it remains favored based on prior baseline evidence (high planarity proxy and a very bright lowest vertical excitation with lowest_state_is_bright). The top2 challenger (TICT) is also not newly weakened by photophysical trends—its plausibility persists structurally (10 rotatable bonds) but remains unsupported by the missing torsion-dependent brightness switching that would be diagnostic. Key remaining discriminator: whether twisting key dihedrals near the heteroaryl (nsnc) core induces strong suppression of f1 and/or bright-state switching (TICT) versus retention of an allowed lowest transition (ICT). An internal pairwise discriminative task for ICT vs TICT has NOT been completed for the current pair (attempts failed), so the best next action is to rerun a bounded microscopic torsion-snapshot screen using only allowed preferred_bond_types values to avoid parser failure.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.45

- task_instruction: Microscopic (PAIRWISE DISCRIMINATIVE: ICT vs TICT) — rerun torsion snapshots with parser-safe bond-type vocabulary.

- Pick 2 dihedrals nearest the nsnc-containing heteroaryl unit.
- Use selection.preferred_bond_types drawn ONLY from: heteroaryl-linkage, aryl-vinyl, aryl-aryl (do NOT use 'aryl-heteroaryl'). Prefer 'heteroaryl-linkage' for the closest attachment; second choice can be aryl-vinyl or aryl-aryl in the same conjugation pathway.

Snapshots: total 2 dihedrals × 3 angles = 6 snapshots.
Excitations: vertical excited states with state_count=5 for each snapshot (same low-cost method as baseline).

- A compact table per dihedral with columns: angle_deg, E1_eV, f1, first_bright_state_index, first_bright_E_eV, first_bright_f, lowest_state_is_bright.
- A short torsion-sensitivity summary focused on: (i) does f1 collapse with twist? (ii) does lowest_state_is_bright switch to false at high torsion?

Keep bounded: no S0 re-optimization beyond constrained snapshot generation; no excited-state optimization; no solvent/aggregate modeling.

### Round 4 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=ICT (0.51) vs top2=TICT (0.24). Latest evidence strengthens ICT: the torsion-snapshot screen on a high-relevance heteroaryl-linkage dihedral shows the lowest excited state remains the first bright state across 0/45/90° with only moderate oscillator-strength decrease (f1 ~0.53 -> 0.46) and modest energy shift (~0.23 eV), which is inconsistent with a classic TICT hallmark (twist-induced dark S1 / bright-state switching). This correspondingly weakens the TICT challenger, though TICT remains plausible because other torsional gates (e.g., aryl–vinyl/aryl–aryl junctions) were not tested and conformer diversity is high. A third candidate (neutral aromatic) is slightly supported/held because persistent brightness under twist can also reflect a largely locally-excited aromatic transition. Key remaining discriminator between ICT and TICT: whether other key dihedrals (particularly aryl-vinyl or aryl-aryl junctions closer to the main conjugation path) can induce near-dark S1 or bright-state reordering at large torsion. Internal pairwise discriminative task for ICT vs TICT has now been partially completed (only 1 dihedral, not the requested 2). Best next action is another bounded microscopic torsion-snapshot run targeting a second dihedral class to complete the ICT-vs-TICT discriminator set.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.51

- task_instruction: Microscopic (PAIRWISE DISCRIMINATIVE: ICT vs TICT) — complete torsion-snapshot screen by targeting a *second* dihedral (different bond-type) beyond the already-tested heteroaryl-linkage.

Base geometry: reuse the same prepared/round_s0_optimized_geometry used in the successful round_04 torsion snapshots.

- Exclude the previously used dihedral_id=dih_0_1_2_3 (or exclude dihedral atom set [0,1,2,3]) to force a different torsion.
- Preferred bond types (allowed literals only): ["aryl-vinyl", "aryl-aryl"].
- Prefer a dihedral on the main conjugation pathway adjacent to (or one bond removed from) the nsnc-containing unit; avoid peripheral phenyl rotors.

- Per-angle table: angle_deg, E1_eV, f1, first_bright_state_index, first_bright_E_eV, first_bright_f, lowest_state_is_bright.
- Explicit comparison to prior heteroaryl-linkage result: does this second torsion show (i) f1 collapse toward ~0 and/or (ii) lowest_state_is_bright switching to false at high torsion? This is the TICT discriminator.

Keep bounded: 1 dihedral × 3 angles; no excited-state optimization; no solvent/aggregate.

### Round 5 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=ICT (0.62) vs top2=neutral aromatic (0.20), with TICT now third (0.16). Latest evidence (microscopic torsion snapshots on an aryl-vinyl dihedral dih_12_13_14_15 at 0/45/90°) strengthens ICT and weakens TICT: S1 remains the first bright state (lowest_state_is_bright) and f1 decreases only moderately from ~0.524 (0°) to ~0.461 (90°) while E1 shifts modestly (~3.43→3.66 eV), providing no bright→dark switching typical of TICT. This shifts the main challenger from TICT toward neutral aromatic/LE-like behavior because persistent brightness under torsion can also reflect LE-dominated transitions in a large polyaryl scaffold. Key remaining discriminator between ICT vs neutral aromatic is explicit evidence of charge-transfer character (electron-hole separation / fragment charge shift) rather than torsion-controlled darkening; current low-cost data mainly report brightness/energies. An internal pairwise discriminative task for the original pair (ICT vs TICT) has now been completed across two torsion classes (heteroaryl-linkage + aryl-vinyl), making the case near closure and best served by an external/verifier-style discriminator focused on ICT vs neutral aromatic (CT character).

### Round 6 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=ICT (0.58) vs top2=neutral aromatic (0.28). Latest evidence (bounded conformer bundle) modestly strengthens ICT but does not decisively eliminate neutral aromatic: across 3 conformers, S1 remains strongly bright (f~1.04–1.06) with extremely small excitation spread (0.0046 eV) and low bright-state sensitivity (0.0171), indicating a robust allowed transition. This robustness is compatible with both a delocalized ICT-like excitation and an LE/neutral-aromatic excitation in a large polyaryl. TICT is further weakened (now third) because two torsion-gate tests show no bright→dark switching. Key remaining discriminator for ICT vs neutral aromatic is direct CT character evidence (electron–hole separation/NTO localization, excited-state dipole change, and/or solvatochromic response), which is not provided by current low-cost outputs. An internal pairwise discriminative task has NOT been completed for the current pair (ICT vs neutral aromatic). The best next action is to run a bounded internal pairwise discriminative task targeting CT-vs-LE diagnostics that are feasible (e.g., frontier orbital localization/fragment charge proxies) and, if insufficient, then escalate to a verifier for external discriminator criteria.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.58

- task_instruction: Microscopic (PAIRWISE DISCRIMINATIVE: ICT vs neutral aromatic) — run the most bounded CT-vs-LE proxy analysis available from existing semiempirical outputs.

Use the existing conformer_bundle artifacts from round_06 (3 conformers) and do NOT run solvent or excited-state optimization.

Tasks (bounded):
1) For each of the 3 conformers, extract and report: S0 dipole magnitude (already available for at least one conformer; report for all if present), and any available excited-state dipole proxy / charge-redistribution proxy from the vertical calculation outputs (if the tool exposes state-wise dipole or transition density/charge metrics).
2) If state-wise dipoles are not available, compute/report a fallback CT proxy using what is available:
   - HOMO and LUMO spatial localization (qualitative) and/or Mulliken charge difference between predefined fragments: (A) the nsnc-containing heteroaryl unit plus its directly attached phenyl, vs (B) the remaining polyaryl framework. Report net fragment charge in S0 and any available excited-state population proxy; if only S0 is available, report fragment HOMO/LUMO localization as a CT-likelihood proxy.
3) Output a compact discriminator verdict: decisive|inconclusive|failed for ICT vs neutral aromatic.

Keep bounded: reuse existing artifacts where possible; avoid any new heavy calculations beyond parsing/deriving these proxies.

- agent_name: microscopic
